
1. REFERENCE TOOLS 

1.1. Bibliographies and Filmographies 

0001	Dian ying zhi nan = Movie guide / Liao Jinfeng bian.
电影指南 = Movie guide / 廖金凤编。
	Shenyang: Liaoning hua bao chu ban she, 2001.	2 v. (2009 p.)
	ISBN	7806014659
Note:	An international filmography with two parts for each film: basic information and a brief film review.
											Chi

0002	Er shi shi ji de dian ying: shi jie dian ying jing dian:1900-2000 = Films of  the century:
     1900-2000 / Wu Guanping zhu bian.
二十世纪的电影：世界电影经典：1900-2000 = Films of the century: 1900-2000 / 吴冠平主编。
	Beijing: San lian shu dian, 2002.	607 p.
	ISBN	7108016427
Note:	A filmography of 260 selected films representing the  world film history in the 20th century.
											Chi

0003	Guo chan yi shu ying pian zi liao hui bian, 1949-1986 / Zhongguo dian ying fa xing fang ying gong si, Hebei sheng dian ying gong si, Zhang Zicheng zhi bi.
国产艺术影片资料汇编，1949-1986 / 中国电影发行放映公司，河北省电影公司，张子成执笔。
Shijiazhuang: Hebei ren min chu ban she, 1988.	1023 p.
ISBN	7202002612
Note:	Includes index.
	A comprehensive filmography of Chinese films produced from 1949-1986.
										Chi

0004	Marion, Donald J.
The Chinese filmography: the 2444 feature films produced by studios in the People's Republic of China from 1949 through 1995.
	Jefferson, N.C. :McFarland & Co., 1996. 		580 p.
	ISBN	0786403055 (lib. bdg. : alk. paper) 
	Note: 	Includes bibliographical references (721-723) and an index (725-752).
A very comprehensive filmography with 2444 feature films produced in PRC during 1949-1995.   

Since there are no Chinese character and tune marks for Pinyin romanizaion system used in this book, there are problems to identify the meaning of some words, and, especially,  people's names that have the same spelling in Pinyin romanization system.
											Eng

0005	Zhong wai ying shi ming zuo ci dian / Li Hengji deng zhu bian.
中外影视名作词典 / 李恒基等主编。
	Beijing: Guo ji wen hua chu ban gong si, 1993.	981 p.
	ISBN	7800499642
											Chi

0006	Zhongguo yi shu ying pian bian mu (1949-1979) /Zhongguo dian ying zi liao guan, Zhongguo yi shu yan jiu yuan dian ying yi shu yan jiu suo bian.
中国艺术影片编目 (1949-1979) /中国电影资料馆，中国艺术研究院电影艺术研究所编。
	Beijing: Wen hua yi shu chu ban she, 1981.  2 v.
Note:	Includes a film title index arranged by the character strokes.
This is the most comprehensive filmography of the films (1109 titles) produced in China between 1949-1979, which include feature films, artistic documentary films, opera films, and animated films. It is arranged chronologically.
	There are two animated films produced in 1948 and added to the end of the book.
										Chi
									
1.2. Indexes

0007	Dian ying "Zao chun er yue" "Lin jia pu zi" "Bu ye cheng" tao lun yu pi pan bao kan zi
 	liao pian ming suo yin / Zhongguo ren min da xue tu shu guan bian.

	Beijing: Zhongguo ren min da xue tu shu guan, 1966.	79 p.
	Note:	Not an official publication
An index to the articles criticizing the films of "Zhao chun er yue" "Lin jia pu zi", and  "Bu ye cheng" 
									Chi

刘华亭。

											Chi

0009	Pi pan mei hua zi chan jie ji de ying pian "Lin jia pu zi", "Bu ye cheng" bao kan zi liao
      suo yin / Ningxia Huizu zizhiqu tu shu guan bian.
批判美化资产阶级的影片"林家铺子 "，"不夜城"报刊资料索引 / 宁夏回族自治区图书馆编。
	Yinchuan: Ningxia Huizu zizhiqu tu shu guan, 1965.	19 p.
Note:	An index to the articles published on the newspapers and journals with the subject of criticizing the films "Lin jia pu zi" and "Bu ye cheng" for the films' tendency of beautifying the Chinese capitalists.

	Beijing: Zhongguo dian ying chu ban she, 1994.  1218 p.
	ISBN	7106009849
Note:	An index to the film study articles published on the journals and newspapers in China from 1980-1989. 
      										Chi

0013	Ying pian "Bei guo jiang nan" tao lun bao kan pian ming suo yin / Shanghai she hui ke xue yuan tu shu guan zi liao can kao zu bian.

0022	Slide, Anthony.
     The international film industry: a historical dictionary
	New York: Greenwood press, 1989.	423 p.
	ISBN	0313256357
Note:	Includes an index in the end of the book and a bibliography under each entry. 
As a dictionary for the international film industry, it has limited and often biased information about the Chinese film industry.  However there are some valuable information and statistics about the Chinese film industry in the book , such as those  under the entry " China", and the information about the companies running movie theatres in China during the beginning of the 20th century like The China Cinema Company Ltd. 
									Eng

1.5. Encyclopedias

0038	Cai, Lin.
蔡林。
      She ying da bai ke ci dian.
      摄影大百科辞典。
	Chengdu: Sichuan ke xue ji shu chu ban she, 1994.	1502 p.
	ISBN	7536427611
	Note:	It provides more than 10,000 entries of photography, film and television.
											Chi

0039	Palmer, Bill, 1947-
The encyclopedia of martial arts movies / Bill Palmer, Karen Palmer, and Ric Meyers.
		Metuchen, N.J.: Scarecrow Press, 1995.	465 p.
		ISBN	0810830272 (acid-free paper)
		Note:	Includes bibliographical references (p.417), aliases and a name index.
It provides 3281 entries of the martial arts films produced mainly by Hong Kong, Taiwan, Japan, United States, and China with the related information such as titles, names of the cast, director, producer, film studio, running time, and availability.   The major problems for using this work are that only the English translations are used for all non-English films,  no original names of these films are listed and the names of the Chinese cast are often romanized in nonstandard ways.  Such as the famous Chinese martial arts film star Jet Li by using the standard Pinyin romanization system, his name should be: Li Lianjie, and by using the standard Wade-Giles romanization system, his name should be: Li Lien-chieh, but the name used in this work is: Li Lin-jei, although his popular non-standard English name Jat Lee is quoted in Aliases.  
												Eng

0040	Shi jie dian ying bai ke quan shu /Yan Haiming deng bien yi.
世界电影百科全书 / 杨海明等编译。
	Beijing: She hui ke xue wen xian chu ban she, 1993.	820 p.
	ISBN	7800502031 
Note:	Translated primarily from the [Russian language] "Encyclopedia of the Cinema" published in 1986 by the Soviet Encyclopedia Press. Entries for lesser Soviet and Eastern Block personalities have been deleted and thorough coverage of Chinese (including Hong Kong and Taiwan) film personalities has been added.
											Chi

0041	Xin bian Zhongguo xiao bai ke quan shu, 11: ying shi xi qu juan / Li Yan zhu bian.
新编中国小百科全书，11：影视戏曲卷 / 李岩主编。
	Yanjie: Yanbian ren min chu ban she, 2000.	360 p.
	ISBN	7806484590
											Chi

0042	Zhang, Yingjin.
Encyclopedia of Chinese film /Yingjin Zhang and Zhiwei Xiao ; with additional contributions from Ru-shou Robert Chen ... [et al.] ; edited by Yingjin Zhang.
	London ; New York: Routledge, 1998.   475 p.
	ISBN	0415151686
Note:	Includes six historical essays on China, Hong Kong, and Taiwan as well as their interaction with and relation to the west; bibliographical references (p. 397-411) and three indexes: Title Index, Name Index, and Studio Index; a glossary of Pinyin romanization, Chinese characters, and English equivalents.
										EngChi

0043	Zhongguo da bai ke quan shu: Dian ying / Zhongguo da bai ke quan shu zong bain ji wei yuan hui "dian ying" bian ji wei yuan hui, Zhongguo da bai ke quan shu chu ban she bien ji bu bian.
中国大百科全书：电影 / 中国大百科全书总编辑委员会 "电影" 编辑委员会，中国大百科全书出版社编辑部编。
	Beijing: Zhongguo da bai ke quan shu chu ban she, 1991.      588 p.
	ISBN	7500002998
Note:	Includes index.  A general encyclopedia of the films (including Chinese films).
		Captions of articles in Chinese, English, and Pinyin.
										ChiEng
		 									
0044	Zhongguo ying pian da dian = Encyclopaedia of Chinese films /Zhongguo dian ying yi shu zhong xin, Zhongguo dian ying zi liao guan bian.
中国影片大典 = Encyclopaedia of Chinese films / 中国电影艺术中心， 中国电影资料馆编。
	Beijing: Zhongguo dian ying chu ban she, 1996.   4 v.
	ISBN	710601155X (v. 1)
		7106010952  (v.4)
Note:	It is the most comprehensive Chinese film encyclopaedia, which covers feature films, documentary films, and opera films produced in China since 1905, but excludes those produced in Taiwan, Hong Kong, and by the film institutions and studios established during Japanese invasion (such as Manzhou Yin Hua Xie Hui, Huabei Dian Ying Gu Fen You Xian Gong Si, Zhonghua Lian He Zhi Pian Gu Fen You Xian Gong Si, and Zhonghua Dian Ying Lian He Gu Fen You Xian Gong Si).  

There are an Award Wining Film List arranged chronologically, and three indexes: Film Title Index, Director Index, and Film Studio Index, which are arranged according to the alphabetic order of the Pinyin romanization system. 

	The table of the contents includes the English translations of the film titles.

 The 4 volumes of the encyclopaedia are: 
      v.1.  Gu shi pian, xi qu pian, 1905-1930.
      v.2.  Gu shi pian, xi qu pian, 1931-1949.
      v.3.  Gu shi pian, xi qu pian, 1949-1976.
			v.4.  Gu shi pian, xi qu pian, 1977-1994.
										ChiEng

0070	Cheng, Jihua.
程季华。
Zhongguo dian ying fa zhan shi: chu gao /Cheng Jihua zhu bian ; Cheng Jihua, Li Shaobai, Xing Zuwen bian zhu.
    中国电影发展史：初稿 / 程季华主编 ； 程季华，李少白，邢祖文编著。
	Beijing:  Zhongguo dian ying chu ban she, 1982.   2 v.
Note:  	This is a the most comprehensive work on Chinese film history (1896-1949) written by the Chinese scholars in Mainland China. It represents the Chinese scholars' perspectives of Chinese film history in Mainland China after 1949. Includes a film index for 1336 film titles, a name index for 985 people, and a film list according to its producing studios. 
		
However, there is only a brief description for the period of Chinese film history under Japanese occupation and there is no filmography about the films produced  by the companies or studios controlled or influenced by Japanese during that period in China.  The best complimentary work for the period, in terms of the current Chinese scholars' perspective in Mainland China,  is   Li  Daoxin's work: Zhongguo dian ying shi (1937-1945), published by Shou du shi fan da xue chu ban she, in Beijing, 2000.
										Chi

	Note:	Includes bibliographical references (p. 287-297) and indes.
A comprehensive work on gender and nation in  a century long Chinese film history, there are four parts:
Part I. Early production. From shadow-play to a national cinema ; Reconstructing history: the (im)possible engagement between feminism and postmodernism in Stanley Kwan's Center stage,  Part II. Socialist cinema. Constructing and consuming the revolutionary narratives ; Gender politics and socialist discourse in Xie Jin's The red detachment of women, Part III. The new wave. Screening China: national allegories and international receptions ; The search for male masculinity and sexuality in Zhang Yimou's Ju dou ; Subjected body and gendered identity: female impersonation in Chen Kaige's Farewell my concubine, and Part IV. Women's films. Feminism with Chinese characteristics? ; Desire in difference: female voice and point of view in Hu Mei's Army nurse ; Transgender masquerading in Huang Shuqin's Human, woman, demon.

	New York: Harry N. Abrams, Inc., 2002.		600 p.
	ISBN	0810906066 (Abrams)
		0810903881 (book club:jkt.)
		0810921405 (book club:pbk.)
		0130340499 (PH)
Note:	Includes Bibliography (p. 554-559); Glossary (p.560-564); Filmography (p. 565-579); Index (580-596), and Credits (p.597-600).

	In Chapter 10: Meeting Hollywood's Challenge, under Filmmaking Outside Europe: There is a brief description of the Chinese film history during the period of the 1930s.

	In Chapter 18: Cinema of Liberation, under China: There is an introduction of the development of Chinese films under the Communist government during the 1950s.  Film directors Xie Jin,  Shui Hua, and their films are introduced.

	In Chapter 24: The Global Advance of Cinema, under Cinema of the "Three Chinas": There is an introduction of the development of Chinese films in China, Taiwan, and Hong Kong during the 1980s.  The fifth generation of Chinese directors in China and their films are introduced.  Film directors Wu Tianming (China) and Hou Hsiao-hsien are specifically introduced here.

	In Chapter 27: World Cinema, under Chinese Films: In the 1990s Chinese films have moved into co-production between China, Taiwan, and Hong Kong.  The sixth generation of Chinese directors and their films are introduced here.  Film directors Chen, Kaige, Zhang Yimou, Tian Zhuangzhuang (China), Hou Hisao-Hsien, Edward Yang, Tsai Ming-Liang (Taiwan), and Wong Kar-Wai (Hong Kong) are specifically introduced here.

2.2.6.  Manchuria and Man'ei  (1932-1945):

0231	Baskett, Michael.
     The attractive empire: colonial Asia in Japanese imperial film culture, 1931-1953.
				336 leaves.
	Note:	Thesis (Ph.D.)-University of California, Los Angles, 2000.
Includes bibliographical references (leaves 321-336) and a selected filmography (leaves 303-320).
In Chapter 1: From Film Empire to Greater East Asian Film Sphere, there is  a general introduction of the history of the Manchuria Motion Picture Production and Distribution Co. or Manshū Eiga Kyōkai  (Man'ei), and its film production, also the competition of Chinese films and Japanese films during the colonial period in Taiwan.
In Chapter 3: Imperial Acts-Looking and Acting "Oriental" , there are discussions about the China issue in Japanese film including how to represent the Chinese characters and who should play the Chinese roles during the 1930s and 1940s.

2.3.6. Manchuria Motion Picture Production and Distribution Co. (Man'ei)

0407	Baskett, Michael.
     The attractive empire: colonial Asia in Japanese imperial film culture, 1931-1953.
				336 leaves.
	Note:	Thesis (Ph.D.)-University of California, Los Angles, 2000.
Includes bibliographical references (leaves 321-336) and a selected filmography (leaves 303-320).
In Chapter 1: From Film Empire to Greater East Asian Film Sphere, there is  a general introduction of the history of the Manchuria Motion Picture Production and Distribution Co. or Manshū Eiga Kyōkai  (Man'ei), and its film production, also the competition of Chinese films and Japanese films during the colonial period in Taiwan.
In Chapter 3: Imperial Acts-Looking and Acting "Oriental" , there are discussions about the China issue in Japanese film including how to represent the Chinese characters and who should play the Chinese roles during the 1930s and 1940s.
									Eng

0479	Palmer, Bill, 1947-
The encyclopedia of martial arts movies / Bill Palmer, Karen Palmer, and Ric Meyers.
		Metuchen, N.J.: Scarecrow Press, 1995.	465 p.
		ISBN	0810830272 (acid-free paper)
		Note:	Includes bibliographical references (p.417), aliases and a name index.
It provides 3281 entries of the martial arts films produced mainly by Hong Kong, Taiwan, Japan, United States, and China with the related information such as titles, names of the cast, director, producer, film studio, running time, and availability.   The major problems for using this work are that only the English translations are used for all non-English films,  no original names of these films are listed and the names of the Chinese cast are often romanized in nonstandard ways.  Such as the famous Chinese martial arts film star Jet Li, by using the standard Pinyin romanization system, his name should be: Li Lianjie, and by using the standard Wade-Giles romanization system, his name should be: Li Lien-chieh, but the name used in this work is: Li Lin-jei, although his non-standard English name Jat Lee is quoted in Alias.  
												Eng

6.2.2.  Chinese and Japanese Films

1065	Baskett, Michael.
     The attractive empire: colonial Asia in Japanese imperial film culture, 1931-1953.
				336 leaves.
	Note:	Thesis (Ph.D.)-University of California, Los Angles, 2000.
Includes bibliographical references (leaves 321-336) and a selected filmography (leaves 303-320).
In Chapter 1: From Film Empire to Greater East Asian Film Sphere, there is  a general introduction of the history of the Manchuria Motion Picture Production and Distribution Co. or Manshū Eiga Kyōkai  (Man'ei), and its film production, also the competition of Chinese films and Japanese films during the colonial period in Taiwan.
In Chapter 3: Imperial Acts-Looking and Acting "Oriental" , there are discussions about the China issue in Japanese film including how to represent the Chinese characters and who should play the Chinese roles during the 1930s and 1940s.
									Eng

1066	Cinematic landscapes: observations on the visual arts and cinema of China and Japan /edited by Linda C. Ehrlich and David Desser.
	Austin, TX.: University of Taxes Press, 1994.  345 p.
	ISBN	0292720866 (hbk)
	ISBN	0292720874 (pbk)
Note: 	Includes bibliographical reference (p.327-330), index, and filmography (p.323-326).
	Includes essays of:
	Contrasts in Chinese and Japanese art / Sherman Lee -- Film and the visual arts in China : an introduction / Douglas Wilkerson -- Chinese visual representation : painting and cinema / Hao Dàzheng -- Classical Chinese painting and cinematographic signification / Ní Zhèn -- Post-socialist strategies : an analysis of Yellow earth and Black cannon incident / Chris Berry and Mary Ann Farquhar -- The pain of a half Taoist : Taoist principles, Chinese landscape painting, and King of the children / An Jingfu -- Judou : an experiment in color and portraiture in Chinese cinema / Jenny Kwok Wah Lau -- Film and the visual arts in Japan : an introduction / Thomas Rimer -- The influence of traditional aesthetics on the Japanese film / Donald Richie -- Japanese cinema and the traditional arts : imagery, technique, and cultural context / Sato Tadao -- Genroku chushingura and the primacy of perception / D. William Davis -- Ways of seeing Japanese prints and films : Mizoguchi's Utamaro / Dudley Andrew -- Kobayashi's widescreen aesthetic / Cynthia Contreras -- Playing with form : Ichikawa's An actor's revenge and the "creative print" / Linda C. Ehrlich -- Playing with space : Ozu and two-dimensional design in Japan / Kathe Geist -- Gate of flesh(tones) : color in the Japanese cinema / David Desser.
											Eng

	Note:	Includes bibliographical references (p. 287-297) and indes.
A comprehensive work on gender and nation in Chinese film history, there are four parts:
Part I. Early production. From shadow-play to a national cinema ; Reconstructing history: the (im)possible engagement between feminism and postmodernism in Stanley Kwan's Center stage,  Part II. Socialist cinema. Constructing and consuming the revolutionary narratives ; Gender politics and socialist discourse in Xie Jin's The red detachment of women, Part III. The new wave. Screening China: national allegories and international receptions ; The search for male masculinity and sexuality in Zhang Yimou's Ju dou ; Subjected body and gendered identity: female impersonation in Chen Kaige's Farewell my concubine, and Part IV. Women's films. Feminism with Chinese characteristics? ; Desire in difference: female voice and point of view in Hu Mei's Army nurse ; Transgender masquerading in Huang Shuqin's Human, woman, demon.
									Eng
